I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed/repo. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Dynamic Filter Pushdown is being applied to the wrong table
### Describe the bug

In the following example, the Dynamic Filter Pushdown is built from `t2 (k, v)` and correctly pushed to `t1 (k)`, to reduce the number of scanned rows from `t1`:

```sql
select *
from t1 -- 1M rows, will become the right side
join t2 on t1.k = t2.k
where t2.v = 1000000; -- 1 row, will become the left side

HashJoinExec join_type=Inner build_time=78.306µs, join_time=22.402µs
    DataSourceExec t2.parquet
        predicate=v@1 = 1000000
        output_rows=1
    DataSourceExec t1.parquet
        predicate=DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ k@0 >= 1000000 AND k@0 <= 1000000 ] -- dynamic filter added here
        output_rows=1 -- only returns 1 row
```

Now if the `t2` side is greater than `t1`, then the order of the join switches, as the smaller relation becomes the build side. However, the Dynamic Filter Pushdown is still applied to the right relation (now `t2`) instead of `t1`:

```sql
select *
from t1 -- 1M rows, will become the left side
join t2 on t1.k = t2.k
where t2.v >= 1000000; -- 9M rows, will become the right side

HashJoinExec join_type=Inner build_time=54.3462ms, join_time=2.403µs -- join is more expensive
    DataSourceExec t1.parquet
        output_rows=1000000
    DataSourceExec t2.parquet
        predicate=v@1 >= 1000000 AND DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ k@0 >= 3 AND k@0 <= 999998 ] -- dynamic filter added here
        output_rows=0 -- should be 1, possibly due to issue https://github.com/apache/datafusion/issues/17188
```

### To Reproduce

```sql
copy (select i as k from generate_series(1, 1000000) t(i)) to 't1.parquet';
copy (select i as k, i as v from generate_series(1, 10000000) t(i)) to 't2.parquet';
create external table t1 stored as parquet location 't1.parquet';
create external table t2 stored as parquet location 't2.parquet';

-- works
explain analyze select *
from t1
join t2 on t1.k = t2.k
where t2.v = 1000000;

-- pushed to the wrong relation
explain analyze select *
from t1
join t2 on t1.k = t2.k
where t2.v >= 1000000;
```

### Expected behavior

Dynamic Filter applied to the correct table.

### Additional context

_No response_

</pr_description>

    97	/// Hard-coded seed to ensure hash values from the hash join differ from `RepartitionExec`, avoiding collisions.
    98	const HASH_JOIN_SEED: RandomState =
    99	    RandomState::with_seeds('J' as u64, 'O' as u64, 'I' as u64, 'N' as u64);
   100	
   101	/// HashTable and input data for the left (build side) of a join
   102	struct JoinLeftData {
   103	    /// The hash table with indices into `batch`
   104	    hash_map: Box<dyn JoinHashMapType>,
   105	    /// The input rows for the build side
   106	    batch: RecordBatch,
   107	    /// The build side on expressions values
   108	    values: Vec<ArrayRef>,
   109	    /// Shared bitmap builder for visited left indices
   110	    visited_indices_bitmap: SharedBitmapBuilder,
   111	    /// Counter of running probe-threads, potentially
   112	    /// able to update `visited_indices_bitmap`
   113	    probe_threads_counter: AtomicUsize,
   114	    /// We need to keep this field to maintain accurate memory accounting, even though we don't directly use it.
   115	    /// Without holding onto this reservation, the recorded memory usage would become inconsistent with actual usage.
   116	    /// This could hide potential out-of-memory issues, especially when upstream operators increase their memory consumption.
   117	    /// The MemoryReservation ensures proper tracking of memory resources throughout the join operation's lifecycle.
   118	    _reservation: MemoryReservation,
   119	}
   120	
   121	impl JoinLeftData {
   122	    /// Create a new `JoinLeftData` from its parts
   123	    fn new(
   124	        hash_map: Box<dyn JoinHashMapType>,
   125	        batch: RecordBatch,
   126	        values: Vec<ArrayRef>,
   127	        visited_indices_bitmap: SharedBitmapBuilder,
   128	        probe_threads_counter: AtomicUsize,
   129	        reservation: MemoryReservation,
   130	    ) -> Self {
   131	        Self {
   132	            hash_map,
   133	            batch,
   134	            values,
   135	            visited_indices_bitmap,
   136	            probe_threads_counter,
   137	            _reservation: reservation,
   138	        }
   139	    }
   140	
   141	    /// return a reference to the hash map
   142	    fn hash_map(&self) -> &dyn JoinHashMapType {
   143	        &*self.hash_map
   144	    }
   145	
   146	    /// returns a reference to the build side batch
   147	    fn batch(&self) -> &RecordBatch {
   148	        &self.batch
   149	    }
   150	
   151	    /// returns a reference to the build side expressions values
   152	    fn values(&self) -> &[ArrayRef] {
   153	        &self.values
   154	    }
   155	
   156	    /// returns a reference to the visited indices bitmap
   157	    fn visited_indices_bitmap(&self) -> &SharedBitmapBuilder {
   158	        &self.visited_indices_bitmap
   159	    }
   160	
   161	    /// Decrements the counter of running threads, and returns `true`
   162	    /// if caller is the last running thread
   163	    fn report_probe_completed(&self) -> bool {
   164	        self.probe_threads_counter.fetch_sub(1, Ordering::Relaxed) == 1
   165	    }
   166	}
   167	
   168	#[allow(rustdoc::private_intra_doc_links)]
   169	/// Join execution plan: Evaluates equijoin predicates in parallel on multiple
   170	/// partitions using a hash table and an optional filter list to apply post
   171	/// join.
   172	///
   173	/// # Join Expressions
   174	///
   175	/// This implementation is optimized for evaluating equijoin predicates  (
   176	/// `<col1> = <col2>`) expressions, which are represented as a list of `Columns`
   177	/// in [`Self::on`].
   178	///
   179	/// Non-equality predicates, which can not pushed down to a join inputs (e.g.
   180	/// `<col1> != <col2>`) are known as "filter expressions" and are evaluated
   181	/// after the equijoin predicates.
   182	///
   183	/// # "Build Side" vs "Probe Side"
   184	///
   185	/// HashJoin takes two inputs, which are referred to as the "build" and the
   186	/// "probe". The build side is the first child, and the probe side is the second
   187	/// child.
   188	///
   189	/// The two inputs are treated differently and it is VERY important that the
   190	/// *smaller* input is placed on the build side to minimize the work of creating
   191	/// the hash table.
   192	///
   193	/// ```text
   194	///          ┌───────────┐
   195	///          │ HashJoin  │
   196	///          │           │
   197	///          └───────────┘
   198	///              │   │
   199	///        ┌─────┘   └─────┐
   200	///        ▼               ▼
   201	/// ┌────────────┐  ┌─────────────┐
   202	/// │   Input    │  │    Input    │
   203	/// │    [0]     │  │     [1]     │
   204	/// └────────────┘  └─────────────┘
   205	///
   206	///  "build side"    "probe side"
   207	/// ```
   208	///
   209	/// Execution proceeds in 2 stages:
   210	///
   211	/// 1. the **build phase** creates a hash table from the tuples of the build side,
   212	///    and single concatenated batch containing data from all fetched record batches.
   213	///    Resulting hash table stores hashed join-key fields for each row as a key, and
   214	///    indices of corresponding rows in concatenated batch.
   215	///
   216	/// Hash join uses LIFO data structure as a hash table, and in order to retain
   217	/// original build-side input order while obtaining data during probe phase, hash
   218	/// table is updated by iterating batch sequence in reverse order -- it allows to
   219	/// keep rows with smaller indices "on the top" of hash table, and still maintain
   220	/// correct indexing for concatenated build-side data batch.
   221	///
   222	/// Example of build phase for 3 record batches:
   223	///
   224	///
   225	/// ```text
   226	///
   227	///  Original build-side data   Inserting build-side values into hashmap    Concatenated build-side batch
   228	///                                                                         ┌───────────────────────────┐
   229	///                             hashmap.insert(row-hash, row-idx + offset)  │                      idx  │
   230	///            ┌───────┐                                                    │          ┌───────┐        │
   231	///            │ Row 1 │        1) update_hash for batch 3 with offset 0    │          │ Row 6 │    0   │
   232	///   Batch 1  │       │           - hashmap.insert(Row 7, idx 1)           │ Batch 3  │       │        │
   233	///            │ Row 2 │           - hashmap.insert(Row 6, idx 0)           │          │ Row 7 │    1   │
   234	///            └───────┘                                                    │          └───────┘        │
   235	///                                                                         │                           │
   236	///            ┌───────┐                                                    │          ┌───────┐        │
   237	///            │ Row 3 │        2) update_hash for batch 2 with offset 2    │          │ Row 3 │    2   │
   238	///            │       │           - hashmap.insert(Row 5, idx 4)           │          │       │        │
   239	///   Batch 2  │ Row 4 │           - hashmap.insert(Row 4, idx 3)           │ Batch 2  │ Row 4 │    3   │
   240	///            │       │           - hashmap.insert(Row 3, idx 2)           │          │       │        │
   241	///            │ Row 5 │                                                    │          │ Row 5 │    4   │
   242	///            └───────┘                                                    │          └───────┘        │
   243	///                                                                         │                           │
   244	///            ┌───────┐                                                    │          ┌───────┐        │
   245	///            │ Row 6 │        3) update_hash for batch 1 with offset 5    │          │ Row 1 │    5   │
   246	///   Batch 3  │       │           - hashmap.insert(Row 2, idx 6)           │ Batch 1  │       │        │
   247	///            │ Row 7 │           - hashmap.insert(Row 1, idx 5)           │          │ Row 2 │    6   │
   248	///            └───────┘                                                    │          └───────┘        │
   249	///                                                                         │                           │
   250	///                                                                         └───────────────────────────┘
   251	///
   252	/// ```
   253	///
   254	/// 2. the **probe phase** where the tuples of the probe side are streamed
   255	///    through, checking for matches of the join keys in the hash table.
   256	///
   257	/// ```text
   258	///                 ┌────────────────┐          ┌────────────────┐
   259	///                 │ ┌─────────┐    │          │ ┌─────────┐    │
   260	///                 │ │  Hash   │    │          │ │  Hash   │    │
   261	///                 │ │  Table  │    │          │ │  Table  │    │
   262	///                 │ │(keys are│    │          │ │(keys are│    │
   263	///                 │ │equi join│    │          │ │equi join│    │  Stage 2: batches from
   264	///  Stage 1: the   │ │columns) │    │          │ │columns) │    │    the probe side are
   265	/// *entire* build  │ │         │    │          │ │         │    │  streamed through, and
   266	///  side is read   │ └─────────┘    │          │ └─────────┘    │   checked against the
   267	/// into the hash   │      ▲         │          │          ▲     │   contents of the hash
   268	///     table       │       HashJoin │          │  HashJoin      │          table
   269	///                 └──────┼─────────┘          └──────────┼─────┘
   270	///             ─ ─ ─ ─ ─ ─                                 ─ ─ ─ ─ ─ ─ ─
   271	///            │                                                         │
   272	///
   273	///            │                                                         │
   274	///     ┌────────────┐                                            ┌────────────┐
   275	///     │RecordBatch │                                            │RecordBatch │
   276	///     └────────────┘                                            └────────────┘
   277	///     ┌────────────┐                                            ┌────────────┐
   278	///     │RecordBatch │                                            │RecordBatch │
   279	///     └────────────┘                                            └────────────┘
   280	///           ...                                                       ...
   281	///     ┌────────────┐                                            ┌────────────┐
   282	///     │RecordBatch │                                            │RecordBatch │
   283	///     └────────────┘                                            └────────────┘
   284	///
   285	///        build side                                                probe side
   286	///
   287	/// ```
   288	///
   289	/// # Example "Optimal" Plans
   290	///
   291	/// The differences in the inputs means that for classic "Star Schema Query",
   292	/// the optimal plan will be a **"Right Deep Tree"** . A Star Schema Query is
   293	/// one where there is one large table and several smaller "dimension" tables,
   294	/// joined on `Foreign Key = Primary Key` predicates.
   295	///
   296	/// A "Right Deep Tree" looks like this large table as the probe side on the
   297	/// lowest join:
   298	///
   299	/// ```text
   300	///             ┌───────────┐
   301	///             │ HashJoin  │
   302	///             │           │
   303	///             └───────────┘
   304	///                 │   │
   305	///         ┌───────┘   └──────────┐
   306	///         ▼                      ▼
   307	/// ┌───────────────┐        ┌───────────┐
   308	/// │ small table 1 │        │ HashJoin  │
   309	/// │  "dimension"  │        │           │
   310	/// └───────────────┘        └───┬───┬───┘
   311	///                   ┌──────────┘   └───────┐
   312	///                   │                      │
   313	///                   ▼                      ▼
   314	///           ┌───────────────┐        ┌───────────┐
   315	///           │ small table 2 │        │ HashJoin  │
   316	///           │  "dimension"  │        │           │
   317	///           └───────────────┘        └───┬───┬───┘
   318	///                               ┌────────┘   └────────┐
   319	///                               │                     │
   320	///                               ▼                     ▼
   321	///                       ┌───────────────┐     ┌───────────────┐
   322	///                       │ small table 3 │     │  large table  │
   323	///                       │  "dimension"  │     │    "fact"     │
   324	///                       └───────────────┘     └───────────────┘
   325	/// ```
   326	///
   327	/// # Clone / Shared State
   328	///
   329	/// Note this structure includes a [`OnceAsync`] that is used to coordinate the
   330	/// loading of the left side with the processing in each output stream.
   331	/// Therefore it can not be [`Clone`]
   332	#[derive(Debug)]
   333	pub struct HashJoinExec {
   334	    /// left (build) side which gets hashed
   335	    pub left: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   336	    /// right (probe) side which are filtered by the hash table
   337	    pub right: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   338	    /// Set of equijoin columns from the relations: `(left_col, right_col)`
   339	    pub on: Vec<(PhysicalExprRef, PhysicalExprRef)>,
   340	    /// Filters which are applied while finding matching rows
   341	    pub filter: Option<JoinFilter>,
   342	    /// How the join is performed (`OUTER`, `INNER`, etc)
   343	    pub join_type: JoinType,
   344	    /// The schema after join. Please be careful when using this schema,
   345	    /// if there is a projection,<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you. You should retry this tool after you have searched inside the file with `grep -n` in order to find the line numbers of what you are looking for.</NOTE>

   436	
   437	    fn create_dynamic_filter(on: &JoinOn) -> Arc<DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr> {
   438	        // Extract the right-side keys from the `on` clauses
   439	        let right_keys: Vec<_> = on.iter().map(|(_, r)| Arc::clone(r)).collect();
   440	        // Initialize with a placeholder expression (true) that will be updated when the hash table is built
   441	        Arc::new(DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr::new(right_keys, lit(true)))
   442	    }
   443	
   444	    /// left (build) side which gets hashed
   445	    pub fn left(&self) -> &Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan> {
   446	        &self.left
   447	    }
   448	
   449	    /// right (probe) side which are filtered by the hash table
   450	    pub fn right(&self) -> &Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan> {
   451	        &self.right
   452	    }
   453	
   454	    /// Set of common columns used to join on
   455	    pub fn on(&self) -> &[(PhysicalExprRef, PhysicalExprRef)] {
   456	        &self.on
   457	    }
   458	
   459	    /// Filters applied before join output
   460	    pub fn filter(&self) -> Option<&JoinFilter> {
   461	        self.filter.as_ref()
   462	    }
   463	
   464	    /// How the join is performed
   465	    pub fn join_type(&self) -> &JoinType {

  1107	/// Reads the left (build) side of the input, buffering it in memory, to build a
  1108	/// hash table (`LeftJoinData`)
  1109	#[expect(clippy::too_many_arguments)]
  1110	async fn collect_left_input(
  1111	    random_state: RandomState,
  1112	    left_stream: SendableRecordBatchStream,
  1113	    on_left: Vec<PhysicalExprRef>,
  1114	    metrics: BuildProbeJoinMetrics,
  1115	    reservation: MemoryReservation,
  1116	    with_visited_indices_bitmap: bool,
  1117	    probe_threads_count: usize,
  1118	    dynamic_filter: Option<Arc<DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr>>,
  1119	    on_right: Vec<PhysicalExprRef>,
  1120	) -> Result<JoinLeftData> {
  1121	    let schema = left_stream.schema();
  1122	
  1123	    // This operation performs 2 steps at once:
  1124	    // 1. creates a [JoinHashMap] of all batches from the stream
  1125	    // 2. stores the batches in a vector.
  1126	    let initial = (Vec::new(), 0, metrics, reservation);
  1127	    let (batches, num_rows, metrics, mut reservation) = left_stream
  1128	        .try_fold(initial, |mut acc, batch| async {
  1129	            let batch_size = get_record_batch_memory_size(&batch);
  1130	            // Reserve memory for incoming batch
  1131	            acc.3.try_grow(batch_size)?;
  1132	            // Update metrics
  1133	            acc.2.build_mem_used.add(batch_size);
  1134	            acc.2.build_input_batches.add(1);
  1135	            acc.2.build_input_rows.add(batch.num_rows());
  1136	            // Update row count
  1137	            acc.1 += batch.num_rows();
  1138	            // Push batch to output
  1139	            acc.0.push(batch);
  1140	            Ok(acc)
  1141	        })
  1142	        .await?;
  1143	
  1144	    // Estimation of memory size, required for hashtable, prior to allocation.
  1145	    // Final result can be verified using `RawTable.allocation_info()`
  1146	    let fixed_size_u32 = size_of::<JoinHashMapU32>();
  1147	    let fixed_size_u64 = size_of::<JoinHashMapU64>();
  1148	
  1149	    // Use `u32` indices for the JoinHashMap when num_rows ≤ u32::MAX, otherwise use the
  1150	    // `u64` indice variant
  1151	    let mut hashmap: Box<dyn JoinHashMapType> = if num_rows > u32::MAX as usize {
  1152	        let estimated_hashtable_size =
  1153	            estimate_memory_size::<(u64, u64)>(num_rows, fixed_size_u64)?;
  1154	        reservation.try_grow(estimated_hashtable_size)?;
  1155	        metrics.build_mem_used.add(estimated_hashtable_size);
  1156	        Box::new(JoinHashMapU64::with_capacity(num_rows))
  1157	    } else {
  1158	        let estimated_hashtable_size =
  1159	            estimate_memory_size::<(u32, u64)>(num_rows, fixed_size_u32)?;
  1160	        reservation.try_grow(estimated_hashtable_size)?;
  1161	        metrics.build_mem_used.add(estimated_hashtable_size);
  1162	        Box::new(JoinHashMapU32::with_capacity(num_rows))
  1163	    };
  1164	
  1165	    let mut hashes_buffer = Vec::new();
  1166	    let mut offset = 0;
  1167	
  1168	    // Updating hashmap starting from the last batch
  1169	    let batches_iter = batches.iter().rev();
  1170	    for batch in batches_iter.clone() {
  1171	        hashes_buffer.clear();
  1172	        hashes_buffer.resize(batch.num_rows(), 0);
  1173	        update_hash(
  1174	            &on_left,
  1175	            batch,
  1176	            &mut *hashmap,
  1177	            offset,
  1178	            &random_state,
  1179	            &mut hashes_buffer,
  1180	            0,
  1181	            true,
  1182	        )?;
  1183	        offset += batch.num_rows();
  1184	    }
  1185	    // Merge all batches into a single batch, so we can directly index into the arrays
  1186	    let single_batch = concat_batches(&schema, batches_iter)?;
  1187	
  1188	    // Reserve additional memory for visited indices bitmap and create shared builder

  1191	        reservation.try_grow(bitmap_size)?;
  1192	        metrics.build_mem_used.add(bitmap_size);
  1193	
  1194	        let mut bitmap_buffer = BooleanBufferBuilder::new(single_batch.num_rows());
  1195	        bitmap_buffer.append_n(num_rows, false);
  1196	        bitmap_buffer

  1198	        BooleanBufferBuilder::new(0)
  1199	    };

    18	//! Filter Pushdown Optimization Process
    19	//!
    20	//! The filter pushdown mechanism involves four key steps:
    21	//! 1. **Optimizer Asks Parent for a Filter Pushdown Plan**: The optimizer calls [`ExecutionPlan::gather_filters_for_pushdown`]
    22	//!    on the parent node, passing in parent predicates and phase. The parent node creates a [`FilterDescription`]
    23	//!    by inspecting its logic and children's schemas, determining which filters can be pushed to each child.
    24	//! 2. **Optimizer Executes Pushdown**: The optimizer recursively pushes down filters for each child,
    25	//!    passing the appropriate filters (`Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>`) for that child.
    26	//! 3. **Optimizer Gathers Results**: The optimizer collects [`FilterPushdownPropagation`] results from children,
    27	//!    containing information about which filters were successfully pushed down vs. unsupported.
    28	//! 4. **Parent Responds**: The optimizer calls [`ExecutionPlan::handle_child_pushdown_result`] on the parent,
    29	//!    passing a [`ChildPushdownResult`] containing the aggregated pushdown outcomes. The parent decides
    30	//!    how to handle filters that couldn't be pushed down (e.g., keep them as FilterExec nodes).
    31	//!
    32	//! [`ExecutionPlan::gather_filters_for_pushdown`]: crate::ExecutionPlan::gather_filters_for_pushdown
    33	//! [`ExecutionPlan::handle_child_pushdown_result`]: crate::ExecutionPlan::handle_child_pushdown_result
    34	//!
    35	//! See also datafusion/physical-optimizer/src/filter_pushdown.rs.
    36	
    37	use std::collections::HashSet;
    38	use std::sync::Arc;
    39	
    40	use datafusion_common::Result;
    41	use datafusion_physical_expr::utils::{collect_columns, reassign_predicate_columns};
    42	use datafusion_physical_expr_common::physical_expr::PhysicalExpr;
    43	use itertools::Itertools;
    44	
    45	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
    46	pub enum FilterPushdownPhase {
    47	    /// Pushdown that happens before most other optimizations.
    48	    /// This pushdown allows static filters that do not reference any [`ExecutionPlan`]s to be pushed down.
    49	    /// Filters that reference an [`ExecutionPlan`] cannot be pushed down at this stage since the whole plan tree may be rewritten
    50	    /// by other optimizations.
    51	    /// Implementers are however allowed to modify the execution plan themselves during this phase, for example by returning a completely
    52	    /// different [`ExecutionPlan`] from [`ExecutionPlan::handle_child_pushdown_result`].
    53	    ///
    54	    /// Pushdown of [`FilterExec`] into `DataSourceExec` is an example of a pre-pushdown.
    55	    /// Unlike filter pushdown in the logical phase, which operates on the logical plan to push filters into the logical table scan,
    56	    /// the `Pre` phase in the physical plan targets the actual physical scan, pushing filters down to specific data source implementations.
    57	    /// For example, Parquet supports filter pushdown to reduce data read during scanning, while CSV typically does not.
    58	    ///
    59	    /// [`ExecutionPlan`]: crate::ExecutionPlan
    60	    /// [`FilterExec`]: crate::filter::FilterExec
    61	    /// [`ExecutionPlan::handle_child_pushdown_result`]: crate::ExecutionPlan::handle_child_pushdown_result
    62	    Pre,
    63	    /// Pushdown that happens after most other optimizations.
    64	    /// This stage of filter pushdown allows filters that reference an [`ExecutionPlan`] to be pushed down.
    65	    /// Since subsequent optimizations should not change the structure of the plan tree except for calling [`ExecutionPlan::with_new_children`]
    66	    /// (which generally preserves internal references) it is safe for references between [`ExecutionPlan`]s to be established at this stage.
    67	    ///
    68	    /// This phase is used to link a [`SortExec`] (with a TopK operator) or a [`HashJoinExec`] to a `DataSourceExec`.
    69	    ///
    70	    /// [`ExecutionPlan`]: crate::ExecutionPlan
    71	    /// [`ExecutionPlan::with_new_children`]: crate::ExecutionPlan::with_new_children
    72	    /// [`SortExec`]: crate::sorts::sort::SortExec
    73	    /// [`HashJoinExec`]: crate::joins::HashJoinExec
    74	    /// [`ExecutionPlan::handle_child_pushdown_result`]: crate::ExecutionPlan::handle_child_pushdown_result
    75	    Post,
    76	}
    77	
    78	impl std::fmt::Display for FilterPushdownPhase {
    79	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> std::fmt::Result {
    80	        match self {
    81	            FilterPushdownPhase::Pre => write!(f, "Pre"),
    82	            FilterPushdownPhase::Post => write!(f, "Post"),
    83	        }
    84	    }
    85	}
    86	
    87	/// The result of a plan for pushing down a filter into a child node.
    88	/// This contains references to filters so that nodes can mutate a filter
    89	/// before pushing it down to a child node (e.g. to adjust a projection)
    90	/// or can directly take ownership of filters that their children
    91	/// could not handle.
    92	#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
    93	pub struct PushedDownPredicate {
    94	    pub discriminant: PushedDown,
    95	    pub predicate: Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>,
    96	}
    97

   100	    pub fn into_inner(self) -> Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr> {

  1063	    fn handle_child_pushdown_result(
  1064	        &self,
  1065	        _phase: FilterPushdownPhase,
  1066	        child_pushdown_result: ChildPushdownResult,
  1067	        _config: &ConfigOptions,
  1068	    ) -> Result<FilterPushdownPropagation<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>>> {
  1069	        // Note: this check shouldn't be necessary because we already marked all parent filters as unsupported for
  1070	        // non-inner joins in `gather_filters_for_pushdown`.
  1071	        // However it's a cheap check and serves to inform future devs touching this function that they need to be really
  1072	        // careful pushing down filters through non-inner joins.
  1073	        if self.join_type != JoinType::Inner {
  1074	            // Other types of joins can support *some* filters, but restrictions are complex and error prone.
  1075	            // For now we don't support them.
  1076	            // See the logical optimizer rules for more details: datafusion/optimizer/src/push_down_filter.rs
  1077	            return Ok(FilterPushdownPropagation::all_unsupported(
  1078	                child_pushdown_result,
  1079	            ));
  1080	        }
  1081	        Ok(FilterPushdownPropagation::if_any(child_pushdown_result))
  1082	    }
  1083	}

  1085	/// Compute min/max bounds for each column in the given arrays
  1086	fn compute_bounds(arrays: &[ArrayRef]) -> Result<Vec<(ScalarValue, ScalarValue)>> {
  1087	    arrays
  1088	        .iter()
  1089	        .map(|array| {
  1090	            if array.is_empty() {
  1091	                // Return NULL values for empty arrays
  1092	                return Ok((
  1093	                    ScalarValue::try_from(array.data_type())?,
  1094	                    ScalarValue::try_from(array.data_type())?,
  1095	                ));
  1096	            }
  1097	
  1098	            // Use Arrow kernels for efficient min/max computation
  1099	            let min_val = min_batch(array)?;
  1100	            let max_val = max_batch(array)?;
  1101	
  1102	            Ok((min_val, max_val))
  1103	        })
  1104	        .collect()
  1105	}
  1106	
  1107	/// Reads the left (build) side of the input, buffering it in memory, to build a
  1108	/// hash table (`LeftJoinData`)
  1109	#[expect(clippy::too_many_arguments)]
  1110	async fn collect_left_input(
  1111	    random_state: RandomState,
  1112	    left_stream: SendableRecordBatchStream,
  1113	    on_left: Vec<PhysicalExprRef>,
  1114	    metrics: BuildProbeJoinMetrics,
  1115	    reservation: MemoryReservation,
  1116	    with_visited_indices_bitmap: bool,
  1117	    probe_threads_count: usize,
  1118	    dynamic_filter: Option<Arc<DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr>>,
  1119	    on_right: Vec<PhysicalExprRef>,
  1120	) -> Result<JoinLeftData> {
  1121	    let schema = left_stream.schema();
  1122	
  1123	    // This operation performs 2 steps at once:
  1124	    // 1. creates a [JoinHashMap] of all batches from the stream
  1125	    // 2. stores the batches in a vector.
  1126	    let initial = (Vec::new(), 0, metrics, reservation);
  1127	    let (batches, num_rows, metrics, mut reservation) = left_stream
  1128	        .try_fold(initial, |mut acc, batch| async {
  1129	            let batch_size = get_record_batch_memory_size(&batch);
  1130	            // Reserve memory for incoming batch
  1131	            acc.3.try_grow(batch_size)?;
  1132	            // Update metrics
  1133	            acc.2.build_mem_used.add(batch_size);
  1134	            acc.2.build_input_batches.add(1);

```rust
// Add actual dynamic filter to right side (probe side)
let dynamic_filter = Arc::clone(&self.dynamic_filter) as Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>;
right_child = right_child.with_self_filter(dynamic_filter);
```

The problem is that regardless of the join swapping that happens during optimization (where smaller table becomes the build side), the dynamic filter is always applied to the right side (probe side). But when the join is swapped, the "right side" conceptually becomes the smaller table, but the dynamic filter should still be applied to the larger table.

"""Script to reproduce the dynamic filter pushdown issue."""

import os

import sys

def run_sql_test():
    """Run SQL test to reproduce the issue."""
    
    # Create temporary directory for test files
    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:

        test_script = f"""
        CREATE EXTERNAL TABLE t1 STORED AS PARQUET LOCATION '"'"'{t1_path}'"'"';
        CREATE EXTERNAL TABLE t2 STORED AS PARQUET LOCATION '"'"'{t2_path}'"'"';
        
        -- Test 1: Normal case (t1 small, t2 large with filter)
        EXPLAIN ANALYZE SELECT * FROM t1 JOIN t2 ON t1.k = t2.k WHERE t2.v = 1000000;
        
        -- Test 2: Swapped case (t2 side larger with more restrictive filter)
        EXPLAIN ANALYZE SELECT * FROM t1 JOIN t2 ON t1.k = t2.k WHERE t2.v >= 1000000;
        """
        
        script_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, "test.sql")
        with open(script_path, "w") as f:
            f.write(test_script)

            # First build the datafusion-cli if needed

                print("STDERR:")
                print(result.stderr)
            
            return result.returncode == 0

            print(f"Error running test: {e}")
            return False

1. Analyzing the issue in HashJoinExec...

Found the problematic code section:
------------------------------------------------------------
Add actual dynamic filter to right side (probe side)
            let dynamic_filter =
                Arc::clone(&self.dynamic_filter) as Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>;
            right_child = right_child.with_self_filter(dynamic_filter)
------------------------------------------------------------

The issue: Dynamic filter is always applied to the 'right' side (probe side)
But when the join order is swapped, the dynamic filter should be applied to the build side
Currently, it's applied to the probe side regardless of which table is actually larger.

Dynamic filter creation logic:
------------------------------------------------------------
fn create_dynamic_filter(on: &JoinOn) -> Arc<DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr> {
        // Extract the right-side keys from the `on` clauses
        let right_keys: Vec<_> = on.iter().map(|(_, r)| Arc::clone(r)).collect();
        // Initialize with a placeholder expression (true) that will be updated when the hash table is built
        Arc::new(DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr::new(right_keys, lit(true)))
------------------------------------------------------------

The dynamic filter is created using right_keys from the join ON clause
This means it's designed to filter the probe side, but the issue is about
which table actually becomes the probe side after join order optimization.

2. Verifying the issue with a simpler approach...

  Contains dynamic filter tests

  Contains dynamic filter tests

3. Conclusion:
The issue is that when the join order is swapped (smaller table becomes build side),
the dynamic filter pushdown logic still applies the filter to the right side (probe side)
instead of correctly identifying which side should be filtered.

   617	    pub fn swap_inputs(
   618	        &self,
   619	        partition_mode: PartitionMode,
   620	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   621	        let left = self.left();
   622	        let right = self.right();
   623	        let new_join = HashJoinExec::try_new(
   624	            Arc::clone(right),
   625	            Arc::clone(left),
   626	            self.on()
   627	                .iter()
   628	                .map(|(l, r)| (Arc::clone(r), Arc::clone(l)))
   629	                .collect(),
   630	            self.filter().map(JoinFilter::swap),
   631	            &self.join_type().swap(),
   632	            swap_join_projection(
   633	                left.schema().fields().len(),
   634	                right.schema().fields().len(),
   635	                self.projection.as_ref(),
   636	                self.join_type(),
   637	            ),
   638	            partition_mode,
   639	            self.null_equality(),
   640	        )?;
   641	        // In case of anti / semi joins or if there is embedded projection in HashJoinExec, output column order is preserved, no need to add projection again
   642	        if matches!(
   643	            self.join_type(),
   644	            JoinType::LeftSemi
   645	                | JoinType::RightSemi
   646	                | JoinType::LeftAnti
   647	                | JoinType::RightAnti
   648	        ) || self.projection.is_some()
   649	        {
   650	            Ok(Arc::new(new_join))
   651	        } else {
   652	            reorder_output_after_swap(Arc::new(new_join), &left.schema(), &right.schema())
   653	        }
   654	    }
   655	}

   437	    fn create_dynamic_filter(on: &JoinOn) -> Arc<DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr> {
   438	        // Extract the right-side keys from the `on` clauses
   439	        let right_keys: Vec<_> = on.iter().map(|(_, r)| Arc::clone(r)).collect();
   440	        // Initialize with a placeholder expression (true) that will be updated when the hash table is built
   441	        Arc::new(DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr::new(right_keys, lit(true)))
   442	    }

2026-01-09 12:05:38,085 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I understand the root cause of the issue!

**The Problem:**
1. When a `HashJoinExec` is created, it automatically creates a dynamic filter using the "right keys" from the join condition.
2. In the filter pushdown logic (line 1053-1055), the dynamic filter is always applied to the "right side" (probe side).
3. However, during optimization, the join order can be swapped if one side is significantly smaller than the other.
4. When the join is swapped using `swap_inputs()`, the left and right sides are reversed, but the dynamic filter logic is not updated.
5. This means the dynamic filter continues to be applied to the "right side", which after swapping becomes the smaller table (the original build side), instead of being applied to the larger table.

**The Fix:**
The dynamic filter should be applied to the **build side** (the smaller table's keys) rather than always to the "right side". However, we need to be careful because:
- The dynamic filter is created using the "right keys"
- When the join is swapped, we need to update which side gets the dynamic filter

Let me look at how the dynamic filter is actually used during execution:

   617	    pub fn swap_inputs(
   618	        &self,
   619	        partition_mode: PartitionMode,
   620	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   621	        let left = self.left();
   622	        let right = self.right();
   623	        let new_join = HashJoinExec::try_new(
   624	            Arc::clone(right),
   625	            Arc::clone(left),
   626	            self.on()
   627	                .iter()
   628	                .map(|(l, r)| (Arc::clone(r), Arc::clone(l)))
   629	                .collect(),
   630	            self.filter().map(JoinFilter::swap),
   631	            &self.join_type().swap(),
   632	            swap_join_projection(
   633	                left.schema().fields().len(),
   634	                right.schema().fields().len(),
   635	                self.projection.as_ref(),
   636	                self.join_type(),
   637	            ),
   638	            partition_mode,
   639	            self.null_equality(),
   640	        )?;
   641	        // In case of anti / semi joins or if there is embedded projection in HashJoinExec, output column order is preserved, no need to add projection again
   642	        if matches!(
   643	            self.join_type(),
   644	            JoinType::LeftSemi
   645	                | JoinType::RightSemi
   646	                | JoinType::LeftAnti
   647	                | JoinType::RightAnti
   648	        ) || self.projection.is_some()
   649	        {
   650	            Ok(Arc::new(new_join))
   651	        } else {
   652	            reorder_output_after_swap(Arc::new(new_join), &left.schema(), &right.schema())
   653	        }
   654	    }
   655	}

"""Script to fix the dynamic filter pushdown issue."""

def analyze_fix():
    print("Analyzing the fix for dynamic filter pushdown issue...")
    print("\n=== PROBLEM ===")

    print("   - Left and right inputs are swapped")
    print("   - Join ON clauses are swapped: (l, r) becomes (r, l)")
    print("   - BUT create_dynamic_filter() ALWAYS uses right keys from ON clauses")

    print("   - But it gets applied to new right side (now probe side)")
    print("   - Filter ends up on wrong table!")
    
    print("\n=== SOLUTION ===")
    print("1. Fix swap_inputs() to handle dynamic filter correctly:")
    print("   - After swapping inputs, we need to swap keys in the dynamic filter")
    print("   - OR create a new dynamic filter using the swapped keys")
    print("\n2. Alternative approach:")
    print("   - Modify create_dynamic_filter() to create filter for build side")
    print("   - Change filter pushdown to apply to build side instead of probe side")

    print("Fix the swap_inputs() method to correctly handle dynamic filter:")
    print("1. When swapping inputs, extract keys from swapped ON clauses")
    print("2. Create new dynamic filter using the build-side keys (which is now the original right side)")
    print("3. This maintains the invariant: dynamic filter always filters the probe side")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    analyze_fix()'

2026-01-09 12:06:46,282 - DEBUG - swea-tools - Retrieved state from environment: {'working_dir': '/testbed/repo'}
2026-01-09 12:06:46,290 - INFO - swea-agent - 🤖 MODEL INPUT
OBSERVATION:

Analyzing the fix for dynamic filter pushdown issue...

=== PROBLEM ===
1. When HashJoinExec.swap_inputs() is called:
   - Left and right inputs are swapped
   - Join ON clauses are swapped: (l, r) becomes (r, l)
   - BUT create_dynamic_filter() ALWAYS uses right keys from ON clauses

2. This means:
   - Dynamic filter is created for original right side (now build side)
   - But it gets applied to new right side (now probe side)
   - Filter ends up on wrong table!

=== SOLUTION ===
1. Fix swap_inputs() to handle dynamic filter correctly:
   - After swapping inputs, we need to swap keys in the dynamic filter
   - OR create a new dynamic filter using the swapped keys

2. Alternative approach:
   - Modify create_dynamic_filter() to create filter for build side
   - Change filter pushdown to apply to build side instead of probe side

=== PREFERRED FIX ===
Fix the swap_inputs() method to correctly handle dynamic filter:
1. When swapping inputs, extract keys from swapped ON clauses
2. Create new dynamic filter using the build-side keys (which is now the original right side)
3. This maintains the invariant: dynamic filter always filters the probe side

        &self,
        partition_mode: PartitionMode,
    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
        let left = self.left();
        let right = self.right();
        
        // Create swapped ON clauses: (original right, original left) -> becomes (new left, new right)
        let swapped_on: Vec<_> = self.on()
            .iter()
            .map(|(l, r)| (Arc::clone(r), Arc::clone(l)))
            .collect();
            
        // Create a new dynamic filter that uses the keys from the new right side (original left side)
        // This ensures the dynamic filter will be applied to the correct side after swapping
        let new_dynamic_filter = Self::create_dynamic_filter(&swapped_on);
        
        // Create the new join with swapped inputs and corrected dynamic filter
        let new_join = HashJoinExec::try_new(
            Arc::clone(right),
            Arc::clone(left),
            swapped_on,
            self.filter().map(JoinFilter::swap),
            &self.join_type().swap(),
            swap_join_projection(
                left.schema().fields().len(),
                right.schema().fields().len(),
                self.projection.as_ref(),
                self.join_type(),
            ),
            partition_mode,
            self.null_equality(),
        )?;
        
        // Replace the dynamic filter in the new join with the corrected one
        // We need to do this after creation because try_new() creates its own dynamic filter
        let mut new_join = Arc::try_unwrap(new_join)
            .map_err(|_| internal_err!("Failed to unwrap Arc for dynamic filter update"))?;
        new_join.dynamic_filter = new_dynamic_filter;
        
        // In case of anti / semi joins or if there is embedded projection in HashJoinExec, output column order is preserved, no need to add projection again
        if matches!(
            self.join_type(),
            JoinType::LeftSemi
                | JoinType::RightSemi
                | JoinType::LeftAnti
                | JoinType::RightAnti
        ) || self.projection.is_some()
        {
            Ok(Arc::new(new_join))
        } else {
            reorder_output_after_swap(Arc::new(new_join), &left.schema(), &right.schema())
        }
    }'

        &self,
        partition_mode: PartitionMode,
    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
        let left = self.left();
        let right = self.right();
        
        // Create swapped ON clauses correctly: (original left, original right) becomes (new left = original right, new right = original left)
        // So for the new join, left keys come from original right, right keys come from original left
        let swapped_on: Vec<_> = self.on()
            .iter()
            .map(|(l, r)| (Arc::clone(r), Arc::clone(l)))
            .collect();

        let new_join = HashJoinExec::try_new_store_dynamic_filter(
            Arc::clone(right),
            Arc::clone(left),
            swapped_on.clone(),
            self.filter().map(JoinFilter::swap),
            &self.join_type().swap(),
            swap_join_projection(
                left.schema().fields().len(),
                right.schema().fields().len(),
                self.projection.as_ref(),
                self.join_type(),
            ),
            partition_mode,
            self.null_equality(),
            // Create dynamic filter using the correct keys for the swapped join
            // The dynamic filter should filter the probe side (new right = original left)
            // So we need to use the right keys from the swapped ON clauses (which are original left keys)
            Self::create_dynamic_filter(&swapped_on),
        )?;
        
        // In case of anti / semi joins or if there is embedded projection in HashJoinExec, output column order is preserved, no need to add projection again
        if matches!(
            self.join_type(),
            JoinType::LeftSemi
                | JoinType::RightSemi
                | JoinType::LeftAnti
                | JoinType::RightAnti
        ) || self.projection.is_some()
        {
            Ok(Arc::new(new_join))
        } else {
            reorder_output_after_swap(Arc::new(new_join), &left.schema(), &right.schema())
        }
    }'

   659	        {
   660	            Ok(Arc::new(new_join))
   661	        } else {
   662	            reorder_output_after_swap(Arc::new(new_join), &left.schema(), &right.schema())
   663	        }
   664	    }

   378	    pub fn try_new(
   379	        left: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   380	        right: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   381	        on: JoinOn,

   385	        partition_mode: PartitionMode,

   389	        let right_schema = right.schema();

   391	            return plan_err!("On constraints in HashJoinExec should be non-empty");
   392	        }

   400

   402

   405	
   406	        let cache = Self::compute_properties(
   407	            &left,
   408	            &right,
   409	            Arc::clone(&join_schema),
   410	            *join_type,
   411	            &on,
   412	            partition_mode,
   413	            projection.as_ref(),
   414	        )?;
   415	
   416	        let dynamic_filter = Self::create_dynamic_filter(&on);
   417	
   418	        Ok(HashJoinExec {
   419	            left,

But looking at my current fix, I realize that simply swapping the inputs and ON clauses through `try_new()` will actually work correctly because `create_dynamic_filter()` will create the dynamic filter based on the swapped ON clauses.

Let me verify this by checking what happens when we call `try_new()` with swapped ON clauses:

1. Original ON: `(t1.k, t2.k)`
2. After swap: `(t2.k, t1.k)`  
3. `create_dynamic_filter()` will use right keys: `t1.k`
4. So the dynamic filter will correctly filter `t1` (which is now the probe side)

Wait, this should actually work correctly! Let me re-read the original problem description to understand what's actually happening.

The problem described is:
- When `t2` is small and `t1` is large: dynamic filter applied to `t1` (correct)
- When `t2` is large and `t1` is small: join order is swapped, but dynamic filter is still applied to `t2` (wrong)

This suggests the issue is NOT in `swap_inputs()` but rather in how the dynamic filter gets pushed down. Let me check the filter pushdown logic more carefully.

   431	    fn name(&self) -> &str {
   432	        &self.name
   433	    }
   434	
   435	    fn schema_check(&self) -> bool {
   436	        true // Filter pushdown does not change the schema of the plan
   437	    }
   438	}
   439	
   440	fn push_down_filters(
   441	    node: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   442	    parent_predicates: Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>,
   443	    config: &ConfigOptions,
   444	    phase: FilterPushdownPhase,
   445	) -> Result<FilterPushdownPropagation<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>>> {
   446	    let mut parent_filter_pushdown_supports: Vec<Vec<PushedDown>> =
   447	        vec![vec![]; parent_predicates.len()];
   448	    let mut self_filters_pushdown_supports = vec![];
   449	    let mut new_children = Vec::with_capacity(node.children().len());
   450	
   451	    let children = node.children();
   452	
   453	    // Filter out expressions that are not allowed for pushdown
   454	    let parent_filtered = FilteredVec::new(&parent_predicates, allow_pushdown_for_expr);
   455	
   456	    let filter_description = node.gather_filters_for_pushdown(
   457	        phase,
   458	        parent_filtered.items().to_vec(),
   459	        config,
   460	    )?;
   461	
   462	    let filter_description_parent_filters = filter_description.parent_filters();
   463	    let filter_description_self_filters = filter_description.self_filters();
   464	    if filter_description_parent_filters.len() != children.len() {
   465	        return Err(datafusion_common::DataFusionError::Internal(
   466	            format!(
   467	                "Filter pushdown expected FilterDescription to have parent filters for {expected_num_children}, but got {actual_num_children} for node {node_name}",
   468	                expected_num_children = children.len(),
   469	                actual_num_children = filter_description_parent_filters.len(),
   470	                node_name = node.name(),
   471	            ),
   472	        ));
   473	    }
   474	    if filter_description_self_filters.len() != children.len() {
   475	        return Err(datafusion_common::DataFusionError::Internal(
   476	            format!(
   477	                "Filter pushdown expected FilterDescription to have self filters for {expected_num_children}, but got {actual_num_children} for node {node_name}",
   478	                expected_num_children = children.len(),
   479	                actual_num_children = filter_description_self_filters.len(),
   480	                node_name = node.name(),
   481	            ),
   482	        ));
   483	    }
   484	
   485	    for (child_idx, (child, parent_filters, self_filters)) in izip!(
   486	        children,
   487	        filter_description.parent_filters(),
   488	        filter_description.self_filters()
   489	    )
   490	    .enumerate()
   491	    {
   492	        // Here, `parent_filters` are the predicates which are provided by the parent node of
   493	        // the current node, and tried to be pushed down over the child which the loop points
   494	        // currently. `self_filters` are the predicates which are provided by the current node,
   495	        // and tried to be pushed down over the child similarly.
   496	
   497	        // Filter out self_filters that contain volatile expressions and track indices
   498	        let self_filtered = FilteredVec::new(&self_filters, allow_pushdown_for_expr);
   499

Now I understand the issue! The problem is that when `collect_left_input` is called, it's passed `on_right` (the right-side join keys) and the dynamic filter. The dynamic filter is then updated with bounds computed from the **left-side** data (build side), but it's applied to filter the **right-side** (probe side).

However, when the join is swapped, the dynamic filter should be updated with bounds from the **new build side** (which was originally the right side) and applied to filter the **new probe side** (which was originally the left side). 

The key insight is that the dynamic filter mechanism is correct, but the issue is that when the join is swapped, the dynamic filter is not being **recreated** with the correct keys for the new probe side.

1. Original ON: `(t1.k, t2.k)` → Dynamic filter created for `t2.k` (right keys)

    34	/// A dynamic [`PhysicalExpr`] that can be updated by anyone with a reference to it.
    35	///
    36	/// Any `ExecutionPlan` that uses this expression and holds a reference to it internally should probably also
    37	/// implement `ExecutionPlan::reset_state` to remain compatible with recursive queries and other situations where
    38	/// the same `ExecutionPlan` is reused with different data.
    39	#[derive(Debug)]
    40	pub struct DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr {
    41	    /// The original children of this PhysicalExpr, if any.
    42	    /// This is necessary because the dynamic filter may be initialized with a placeholder (e.g. `lit(true)`)
    43	    /// and later remapped to the actual expressions that are being filtered.
    44	    /// But we need to know the children (e.g. columns referenced in the expression) ahead of time to evaluate the expression correctly.
    45	    children: Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>,
    46	    /// If any of the children were remapped / modified (e.g. to adjust for projections) we need to keep track of the new children
    47	    /// so that when we update `current()` in subsequent iterations we can re-apply the replacements.
    48	    remapped_children: Option<Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>>,
    49	    /// The source of dynamic filters.
    50	    inner: Arc<RwLock<Inner>>,

"""Analyze the dynamic filter pushdown issue more carefully."""

def analyze_issue():
    print("=== ANALYSIS OF DYNAMIC FILTER PUSHDOWN ISSUE ===\n")
    
    print("1. ORIGINAL JOIN (t1 small, t2 large with filter):")
    print("   HashJoinExec(left=t1, right=t2)")
    print("   ON clause: [(t1.k, t2.k)]")
    print("   Dynamic filter created using right keys: [t2.k]")
    print("   Filter pushdown: dynamic filter applied to RIGHT (probe) side")
    print("   Result: t2 gets filtered by dynamic filter from t1.k values - CORRECT\n")
    
    print("2. AFTER SWAP (t2 becomes smaller due to WHERE t2.v >= 1000000):")
    print("   HashJoinExec(left=t2, right=t1)")
    print("   ON clause after swap: [(t2.k, t1.k)]")
    print("   Dynamic filter created using right keys from swapped ON: [t1.k]")
    print("   Filter pushdown: dynamic filter applied to NEW RIGHT (probe) side")
    print("   Result: t1 gets filtered by dynamic filter from t2.k values - WRONG!\n")
    
    print("=== THE PROBLEM ===")
    print("The issue is in the filter pushdown logic, not necessarily in swap_inputs().")
    print("After swap:")
    print("- LEFT becomes t2 (the smaller table with restrictive WHERE)")
    print("- RIGHT becomes t1 (the probe side)")
    print("- Dynamic filter should filter t1 based on t2'"'"'s join keys")
    print("\nBut the dynamic filter is created using the WRONG keys:")
    print("- It uses '"'"'right keys'"'"' from the ON clause")
    print("- Original: ON(t1.k, t2.k) -> right key = t2.k")
    print("- After swap: ON(t2.k, t1.k) -> right key = t1.k")
    print("- Problem: t1 should be filtered by t2.k values, not t1.k values")
    
    print("\n=== THE FIX ===")
    print("The dynamic filter should always filter the PROBE side using BUILD side'"'"'s keys.")
    print("We need to fix create_dynamic_filter() to use:")
    print("- LEFT keys when filtering the RIGHT side (normal case)")
    print("- RIGHT keys when filtering the LEFT side (after swap)")
    print("\nBut wait... the current implementation actually creates the filter correctly!")
    print("Because after swap:")
    print("- Build side = t2 (LEFT)")
    print("- Probe side = t1 (RIGHT)")
    print("- Dynamic filter should filter t1 using t2'"'"'s keys")
    print("- And the dynamic filter uses RIGHT keys from the ON clause (t1.k)")
    print("\nThis suggests the issue might be elsewhere...")

    print("In gather_filters_for_pushdown(), we always apply it to the right side:")
    print("  '"'"'Add actual dynamic filter to right side (probe side)'"'"'")
    print("\nBut we need to determine which side is actually the probe side dynamically.")

2026-01-09 12:15:19,481 - DEBUG - swea-tools - Retrieved state from environment: {'working_dir': '/testbed/repo'}
2026-01-09 12:15:19,489 - INFO - swea-agent - 🤖 MODEL INPUT
OBSERVATION:

=== ANALYSIS OF DYNAMIC FILTER PUSHDOWN ISSUE ===

1. ORIGINAL JOIN (t1 small, t2 large with filter):
   HashJoinExec(left=t1, right=t2)
   ON clause: [(t1.k, t2.k)]
   Dynamic filter created using right keys: [t2.k]
   Filter pushdown: dynamic filter applied to RIGHT (probe) side
   Result: t2 gets filtered by dynamic filter from t1.k values - CORRECT

2. AFTER SWAP (t2 becomes smaller due to WHERE t2.v >= 1000000):
   HashJoinExec(left=t2, right=t1)
   ON clause after swap: [(t2.k, t1.k)]
   Dynamic filter created using right keys from swapped ON: [t1.k]
   Filter pushdown: dynamic filter applied to NEW RIGHT (probe) side
   Result: t1 gets filtered by dynamic filter from t2.k values - WRONG!

=== THE PROBLEM ===
The issue is in the filter pushdown logic, not necessarily in swap_inputs().
After swap:
- LEFT becomes t2 (the smaller table with restrictive WHERE)
- RIGHT becomes t1 (the probe side)
- Dynamic filter should filter t1 based on t2's join keys

But the dynamic filter is created using the WRONG keys:
- It uses 'right keys' from the ON clause
- Original: ON(t1.k, t2.k) -> right key = t2.k
- After swap: ON(t2.k, t1.k) -> right key = t1.k
- Problem: t1 should be filtered by t2.k values, not t1.k values

=== THE FIX ===
The dynamic filter should always filter the PROBE side using BUILD side's keys.
We need to fix create_dynamic_filter() to use:
- LEFT keys when filtering the RIGHT side (normal case)
- RIGHT keys when filtering the LEFT side (after swap)

But wait... the current implementation actually creates the filter correctly!
Because after swap:
- Build side = t2 (LEFT)
- Probe side = t1 (RIGHT)
- Dynamic filter should filter t1 using t2's keys
- And the dynamic filter uses RIGHT keys from the ON clause (t1.k)

This suggests the issue might be elsewhere...

=== ALTERNATIVE APPROACH ===
Maybe the issue is in how the dynamic filter is APPLIED, not created.
In gather_filters_for_pushdown(), we always apply it to the right side:
  'Add actual dynamic filter to right side (probe side)'

But we need to determine which side is actually the probe side dynamically.

2026-01-09 12:16:21,612 - INFO - swea-agent - 🤖 MODEL INPUT
OBSERVATION:

=== REANALYSIS OF THE PROBLEM ===

After careful examination, the issue is NOT in swap_inputs().
The dynamic filter creation is actually CORRECT.

The REAL ISSUE is in how filters are pushed down.

Current logic in gather_filters_for_pushdown():
  'Add actual dynamic filter to right side (probe side)'
  This assumes the RIGHT side is ALWAYS the probe side
  But after swap, the RIGHT side becomes the original LEFT side

=== EXAMPLE ===
Original query: SELECT * FROM t1 JOIN t2 ON t1.k = t2.k WHERE t2.v >= 1000000
After optimization:
- t2.v >= 1000000 reduces t2 from 10M to 9M rows
- t1 has 1M rows
- t2 (9M) > t1 (1M), so join gets SWAPPED
- t2 becomes LEFT (build side)
- t1 becomes RIGHT (probe side)

Dynamic filter created using RIGHT keys from swapped ON:
- ON(t2.k, t1.k) -> right key = t1.k
- Filter will be: t1.k >= min(t2.k) AND t1.k <= max(t2.k)
- This should reduce t1 scan based on actual t2.k values

=== BUT THE ISSUE IS ELSEWHERE ===
Looking at the PR description again:
- 'DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ k@0 >= 3 AND k@0 <= 999998 ]'
- Here k@0 refers to t2.k (not t1.k)
- This suggests the filter is being applied to the WRONG table

=== ACTUAL FIX NEEDED ===
The dynamic filter expressions reference COLUMN INDICES, not names.
After swap, the column references need to be RE-MAPPED correctly.

The fix should be:
1. In swap_inputs(), when we swap ON clauses, we also need to
   ensure dynamic filter expressions reference the correct columns.
2. The DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr needs to update its references
   based on the new schema after swap.

=== SIMPLER FIX ===
Actually, the issue might be more fundamental:
The dynamic filter ALWAYS filters the column(s) referenced in its children.
These children are defined when create_dynamic_filter() is called.
After swap, the old dynamic filter still references the original columns.

We need to CREATE A NEW dynamic filter after swap with correct column references.

        &self,
        partition_mode: PartitionMode,
    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
        let left = self.left();
        let right = self.right();
        
        // Create swapped ON clauses correctly: (original left, original right) becomes (new left = original right, new right = original left)
        // So for the new join, left keys come from original right, right keys come from original left
        let swapped_on: Vec<_> = self.on()
            .iter()
            .map(|(l, r)| (Arc::clone(r), Arc::clone(l)))

        // Create new join with swapped inputs
        let new_join = HashJoinExec::try_new(

        &self,
        partition_mode: PartitionMode,
    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
        let left = self.left();
        let right = self.right();
        
        // Create swapped ON clauses correctly: (original left, original right) becomes (new left = original right, new right = original left)
        // So for the new join, left keys come from original right, right keys come from original left
        let swapped_on: Vec<_> = self.on()
            .iter()
            .map(|(l, r)| (Arc::clone(r), Arc::clone(l)))
            .collect();

        // Create new join with swapped inputs
        let mut new_join = HashJoinExec::try_new(
            Arc::clone(right),
            Arc::clone(left),
            swapped_on,
            self.filter().map(JoinFilter::swap),
            &self.join_type().swap(),
            swap_join_projection(
                left.schema().fields().len(),
                right.schema().fields().len(),
                self.projection.as_ref(),
                self.join_type(),
            ),
            partition_mode,
            self.null_equality(),
        )?;

        // After swap, the dynamic filter needs to filter the probe side (which is now the original left side)
        // The dynamic filter should filter the right side using the build side'"'"'s values
        // Since try_new() creates a new dynamic filter based on swapped_on, it should already be correct
        // (it uses right keys from swapped_on, which are the original left keys)
        
        // In case of anti / semi joins or if there is embedded projection in HashJoinExec, output column order is preserved, no need to add projection again
        if matches!(
            self.join_type(),
            JoinType::LeftSemi
                | JoinType::RightSemi
                | JoinType::LeftAnti
                | JoinType::RightAnti
        ) || self.projection.is_some()
        {

   612	    ///
   613	    /// # Notes:
   614	    ///
   615	    /// This function is public so other downstream projects can use it to
   616	    /// construct `HashJoinExec` with right side as the build side.
   617	    pub fn swap_inputs(
   618	        &self,
   619	        partition_mode: PartitionMode,
   620	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   621	        let left = self.left();
   622	        let right = self.right();
   623	        
   624	        // Create swapped ON clauses correctly: (original left, original right) becomes (new left = original right, new right = original left)
   625	        // So for the new join, left keys come from original right, right keys come from original left
   626	        let swapped_on: Vec<_> = self.on()
   627	            .iter()
   628	            .map(|(l, r)| (Arc::clone(r), Arc::clone(l)))
   629	            .collect();
   630	
   631	        // Create new join with swapped inputs
   632	        let mut new_join = HashJoinExec::try_new(
   633	            Arc::clone(right),
   634	            Arc::clone(left),
   635	            swapped_on,
   636	            self.filter().map(JoinFilter::swap),
   637	            &self.join_type().swap(),
   638	            swap_join_projection(
   639	                left.schema().fields().len(),
   640	                right.schema().fields().len(),
   641	                self.projection.as_ref(),
   642	                self.join_type(),
   643	            ),
   644	            partition_mode,
   645	            self.null_equality(),
   646	        )?;
   647	
   648	        // After swap, the dynamic filter needs to filter the probe side (which is now the original left side)
   649	        // The dynamic filter should filter the right side using the build side's values
   650	        // Since try_new() creates a new dynamic filter based on swapped_on, it should already be correct
   651	        // (it uses right keys from swapped_on, which are the original left keys)
   652	        
   653	        // In case of anti / semi joins or if there is embedded projection in HashJoinExec, output column order is preserved, no need to add projection again
   654	        if matches!(
   655	            self.join_type(),
   656	            JoinType::LeftSemi
   657	                | JoinType::RightSemi
   658	                | JoinType::LeftAnti
   659	                | JoinType::RightAnti
   660	        ) || self.projection.is_some()
   661	        {
   662	            Ok(Arc::new(new_join))
   663	        } else {
   664	            reorder_output_after_swap(Arc::new(new_join), &left.schema(), &right.schema())
   665	        }
   666	    }
   667	}
   668

The key insight is that dynamic filters use column references (like `k@0`) which are based on the schema of the table being filtered. When the join order is swapped, these column references need to be updated to point to the correct columns in the new schema.

   200	    /// - After every batch is processed if we update the TopK heap in a SortExec using a TopK approach.
   201	    pub fn update(&self, new_expr: Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>) -> Result<()> {
   202	        let mut current = self.inner.write().map_err(|_| {
   203	            datafusion_common::DataFusionError::Execution(
   204	                "Failed to acquire write lock for inner".to_string(),
   205	            )
   206	        })?;
   207	        // Remap the children of the new expression to match the original children
   208	        // We still do this again in `current()` but doing it preventively here
   209	        // reduces the work needed in some cases if `current()` is called multiple times
   210	        // and the same externally facing `PhysicalExpr` is used for both `with_new_children` and `update()`.`
   211	        let new_expr = Self::remap_children(
   212	            &self.children,
   213	            self.remapped_children.as_ref(),
   214	            new_expr,
   215	        )?;
   216	        // Update the inner expression to the new expression.
   217	        current.expr = new_expr;
   218	        // Increment the generation to indicate that the expression has changed.
   219	        current.generation += 1;
   220	        Ok(())
   221	    }
   222	}
   223	
   224	impl PhysicalExpr for DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr {
   225	    fn as_any(&self) -> &dyn Any {
   226	        self
   227	    }
   228	
   229	    fn children(&self) -> Vec<&Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>> {
   230	        self.remapped_children
   231	            .as_ref()
   232	            .unwrap_or(&self.children)
   233	            .iter()
   234	            .collect()
   235	    }
   236	
   237	    fn with_new_children(
   238	        self: Arc<Self>,
   239	        children: Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>,
   240	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>> {
   241	        Ok(Arc::new(Self {
   242	            children: self.children.clone(),
   243	            remapped_children: Some(children),
   244	            inner: Arc::clone(&self.inner),
   245	            data_type: Arc::clone(&self.data_type),
   246	            nullable: Arc::clone(&self.nullable),
   247	        }))
   248	    }

"""Identify the final fix needed for dynamic filter pushdown."""

def identify_fix():

    print("2. create_dynamic_filter() is CORRECT - it uses right keys from ON clauses")

    print("- But the dynamic filter should be applied to t1 (RIGHT side)")
    print("- k@0 should refer to t1.k NOT t2.k\n")
    
    print("=== THE REAL PROBLEM ===")
    print("The DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr references column indices in the build side schema")
    print("But when applied to the probe side, those column indices are INCORRECT")

    print("- t1 has schema: [k] -> k index 0")

2026-01-09 12:18:57,821 - INFO - swea-agent - 🤖 MODEL INPUT
OBSERVATION:

=== FINAL ANALYSIS OF THE PROBLEM ===

After detailed examination:
1. swap_inputs() is CORRECT - it creates proper swapped ON clauses
2. create_dynamic_filter() is CORRECT - it uses right keys from ON clauses
3. The issue is in column reference resolution after swap

=== THE ACTUAL ISSUE ===
When the optimizer swaps the join:
- Dynamic filter is created using right_keys from swapped ON
- After swap: ON(t2.k, t1.k) -> dynamic filter uses t1.k
- Filter pushdown applies to right side (probe side) which is t1
- So t1 gets filtered by t2.k values - THIS SHOULD BE CORRECT!

=== WAIT, THE ISSUE IS DIFFERENT ===
Looking at the PR description output:
- 'predicate=v@1 >= 1000000 AND DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ k@0 >= 3 AND k@0 <= 999998 ]'
- k@0 refers to column 0 of t2 (the LEFT side after swap)
- But the dynamic filter should be applied to t1 (RIGHT side)
- k@0 should refer to t1.k NOT t2.k

=== THE REAL PROBLEM ===
The DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr references column indices in the build side schema
But when applied to the probe side, those column indices are INCORRECT

Example after swap:
- t2 has schema: [k, v] -> k index 0
- t1 has schema: [k] -> k index 0
- Dynamic filter references 'k@0' which refers to t2.k index 0
- But when applied to t1, 'k@0' refers to t1.k index 0
- This works by coincidence when both tables have same column structure!

=== THE REAL FIX ===
The issue is NOT in swap_inputs() but in how the dynamic filter is APPLIED.
Currently, the filter pushdown logic assumes the dynamic filter references
columns that exist in the probe side schema with the same indices.

This works ONLY when both sides have the same column structure.
In the PR example, both t1 and t2 have 'k' as their first column.

=== SO THE REAL SOLUTION ===
The dynamic filter EXPRESSION ITSELF needs to be transformed to reference
the correct column indices in the probe side schema.

This should happen during filter pushdown, not during join swapping.

=== ACTION PLAN ===
1. Check where dynamic filter is applied (gather_filters_for_pushdown)
2. Make sure the dynamic filter expression references correct columns
3. Transform the filter to use probe side column indices

   123	pub enum PushedDown {
   124	    /// The predicate was successfully pushed down into the child node.
   125	    Yes,
   126	    /// The predicate could not be pushed down into the child node.
   127	    No,
   128	}

   130	impl PushedDown {
   131	    /// Logical AND operation: returns `Yes` only if both operands are `Yes`.
   132	    pub fn and(self, other: PushedDown) -> PushedDown {
   133	        match (self, other) {
   134	            (PushedDown::Yes, PushedDown::Yes) => PushedDown::Yes,
   135	            _ => PushedDown::No,
   136	        }
   137	    }
   138

   140	    pub fn or(self, other: PushedDown) -> PushedDown {
   141	        match (self, other) {
   142	            (PushedDown::Yes, _) | (_, PushedDown::Yes) => PushedDown::Yes,
   143	            (PushedDown::No, PushedDown::No) => PushedDown::No,
   144	        }
   145	    }

+#!/usr/bin/env python3

+def analyze_issue():

+    
+    print("1. ORIGINAL JOIN (t1 small, t2 large with filter):")
+    print("   HashJoinExec(left=t1, right=t2)")
+    print("   ON clause: [(t1.k, t2.k)]")
+    print("   Dynamic filter created using right keys: [t2.k]")
+    print("   Filter pushdown: dynamic filter applied to RIGHT (probe) side")
+    print("   Result: t2 gets filtered by dynamic filter from t1.k values - CORRECT\n")
+    
+    print("2. AFTER SWAP (t2 becomes smaller due to WHERE t2.v >= 1000000):")
+    print("   HashJoinExec(left=t2, right=t1)")
+    print("   ON clause after swap: [(t2.k, t1.k)]")
+    print("   Dynamic filter created using right keys from swapped ON: [t1.k]")
+    print("   Filter pushdown: dynamic filter applied to NEW RIGHT (probe) side")
+    print("   Result: t1 gets filtered by dynamic filter from t2.k values - WRONG!\n")
+    
+    print("=== THE PROBLEM ===")
+    print("The issue is in the filter pushdown logic, not necessarily in swap_inputs().")
+    print("After swap:")
+    print("- LEFT becomes t2 (the smaller table with restrictive WHERE)")
+    print("- RIGHT becomes t1 (the probe side)")
+    print("- Dynamic filter should filter t1 based on t2's join keys")
+    print("\nBut the dynamic filter is created using the WRONG keys:")
+    print("- It uses 'right keys' from the ON clause")
+    print("- Original: ON(t1.k, t2.k) -> right key = t2.k")
+    print("- After swap: ON(t2.k, t1.k) -> right key = t1.k")
+    print("- Problem: t1 should be filtered by t2.k values, not t1.k values")
+    
+    print("\n=== THE FIX ===")
+    print("The dynamic filter should always filter the PROBE side using BUILD side's keys.")
+    print("We need to fix create_dynamic_filter() to use:")
+    print("- LEFT keys when filtering the RIGHT side (normal case)")
+    print("- RIGHT keys when filtering the LEFT side (after swap)")
+    print("\nBut wait... the current implementation actually creates the filter correctly!")
+    print("Because after swap:")
+    print("- Build side = t2 (LEFT)")
+    print("- Probe side = t1 (RIGHT)")
+    print("- Dynamic filter should filter t1 using t2's keys")
+    print("- And the dynamic filter uses RIGHT keys from the ON clause (t1.k)")
+    print("\nThis suggests the issue might be elsewhere...")
+    
+    print("\n=== ALTERNATIVE APPROACH ===")
+    print("Maybe the issue is in how the dynamic filter is APPLIED, not created.")
+    print("In gather_filters_for_pushdown(), we always apply it to the right side:")
+    print("  'Add actual dynamic filter to right side (probe side)'")
+    print("\nBut we need to determine which side is actually the probe side dynamically.")
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    analyze_issue()

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+"""Identify the final fix needed for dynamic filter pushdown."""
+
+def identify_fix():
+    print("=== FINAL ANALYSIS OF THE PROBLEM ===\n")
+    
+    print("After detailed examination:")
+    print("1. swap_inputs() is CORRECT - it creates proper swapped ON clauses")
+    print("2. create_dynamic_filter() is CORRECT - it uses right keys from ON clauses")
+    print("3. The issue is in column reference resolution after swap\n")
+    
+    print("=== THE ACTUAL ISSUE ===")
+    print("When the optimizer swaps the join:")
+    print("- Dynamic filter is created using right_keys from swapped ON")
+    print("- After swap: ON(t2.k, t1.k) -> dynamic filter uses t1.k")
+    print("- Filter pushdown applies to right side (probe side) which is t1")
+    print("- So t1 gets filtered by t2.k values - THIS SHOULD BE CORRECT!\n")
+    
+    print("=== WAIT, THE ISSUE IS DIFFERENT ===")
+    print("Looking at the PR description output:")
+    print("- 'predicate=v@1 >= 1000000 AND DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ k@0 >= 3 AND k@0 <= 999998 ]'")
+    print("- k@0 refers to column 0 of t2 (the LEFT side after swap)")
+    print("- But the dynamic filter should be applied to t1 (RIGHT side)")
+    print("- k@0 should refer to t1.k NOT t2.k\n")
+    
+    print("=== THE REAL PROBLEM ===")
+    print("The DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr references column indices in the build side schema")
+    print("But when applied to the probe side, those column indices are INCORRECT")
+    print("\nExample after swap:")
+    print("- t2 has schema: [k, v] -> k index 0")
+    print("- t1 has schema: [k] -> k index 0")
+    print("- Dynamic filter references 'k@0' which refers to t2.k index 0")
+    print("- But when applied to t1, 'k@0' refers to t1.k index 0")
+    print("- This works by coincidence when both tables have same column structure!\n")
+    
+    print("=== THE REAL FIX ===")
+    print("The issue is NOT in swap_inputs() but in how the dynamic filter is APPLIED.")
+    print("Currently, the filter pushdown logic assumes the dynamic filter references")
+    print("columns that exist in the probe side schema with the same indices.")
+    print("\nThis works ONLY when both sides have the same column structure.")
+    print("In the PR example, both t1 and t2 have 'k' as their first column.")
+    
+    print("\n=== SO THE REAL SOLUTION ===")
+    print("The dynamic filter EXPRESSION ITSELF needs to be transformed to reference")
+    print("the correct column indices in the probe side schema.")
+    print("\nThis should happen during filter pushdown, not during join swapping.")
+    
+    print("\n=== ACTION PLAN ===")
+    print("1. Check where dynamic filter is applied (gather_filters_for_pushdown)")
+    print("2. Make sure the dynamic filter expression references correct columns")
+    print("3. Transform the filter to use probe side column indices")
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    identify_fix()

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+"""Script to fix the dynamic filter pushdown issue."""
+
+def analyze_fix():
+    print("Analyzing the fix for dynamic filter pushdown issue...")
+    print("\n=== PROBLEM ===")
+    print("1. When HashJoinExec.swap_inputs() is called:")
+    print("   - Left and right inputs are swapped")
+    print("   - Join ON clauses are swapped: (l, r) becomes (r, l)")
+    print("   - BUT create_dynamic_filter() ALWAYS uses right keys from ON clauses")
+    print("\n2. This means:")
+    print("   - Dynamic filter is created for original right side (now build side)")
+    print("   - But it gets applied to new right side (now probe side)")
+    print("   - Filter ends up on wrong table!")
+    
+    print("\n=== SOLUTION ===")
+    print("1. Fix swap_inputs() to handle dynamic filter correctly:")
+    print("   - After swapping inputs, we need to swap keys in the dynamic filter")
+    print("   - OR create a new dynamic filter using the swapped keys")
+    print("\n2. Alternative approach:")
+    print("   - Modify create_dynamic_filter() to create filter for build side")
+    print("   - Change filter pushdown to apply to build side instead of probe side")
+    
+    print("\n=== PREFERRED FIX ===")
+    print("Fix the swap_inputs() method to correctly handle dynamic filter:")
+    print("1. When swapping inputs, extract keys from swapped ON clauses")
+    print("2. Create new dynamic filter using the build-side keys (which is now the original right side)")
+    print("3. This maintains the invariant: dynamic filter always filters the probe side")
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    analyze_fix()
